  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_cfd96c5d-4a2b-4e00-98c2-1f261adee708'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer9679617506098410653">Aku ingin mendaki puncak tantangan, menerjang batu granit kesulitan, menggoda mara bahaya, dan memecahkan misteri dengan sains. Aku ingin menghirup berupa-rupa pengalaman lalu terjun bebas menyelami labirin lika-liku hidup yang ujungnya tak dapat disangka. Aku mendamba kehidupan dengan kemungkinan-kemungkinan yang bereaksi satu sama lain seperti benturan molekul uranium: m</span>
  <span id="freeText9679617506098410653" style="display:none">Aku ingin mendaki puncak tantangan, menerjang batu granit kesulitan, menggoda mara bahaya, dan memecahkan misteri dengan sains. Aku ingin menghirup berupa-rupa pengalaman lalu terjun bebas menyelami labirin lika-liku hidup yang ujungnya tak dapat disangka. Aku mendamba kehidupan dengan kemungkinan-kemungkinan yang bereaksi satu sama lain seperti benturan molekul uranium: meletup tak terduga-duga, menyerap, mengikat, mengganda, berkembang, terurai, dan berpencar ke arah yang mengejutkan. Aku ingin ke tempat-tempat yang jauh, menjumpai beragam bahasa dan orang-orang asing. Aku ingin berkelana, menemukan arahku dengan membaca bintang gemintang. Aku ingin mengarungi padang dan gurun-gurun, ingin melepuh terbakar matahari, limbung dihantam angin, dan menciut dicengkeram dingin. Aku ingin kehidupan yang menggetarkan, penuh dengan penaklukan. Aku ingin hidup! Ingin merasakan sari pati hidup!</span>
  <a data-text-id="9679617506098410653" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_9172766" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/9172766" />
    <a title="Ambar" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/213286-ambar"><img alt="Ambar" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1259264637p2/213286.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/9172766?book_show_action=true">Nov 15, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ambar" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ambar" href="/user/show/213286-ambar">Ambar</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">anyone who want to inspire about backpacking</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/213286-ambar?shelf=travel">travel</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/213286-ambar?shelf=indonesia">indonesia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer9172766" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12448587451394266578">I read Edensor after the first tetra-logy of Andrea Hirata Laskar Pelangi (LP). Only take few hours I came to conclusions that Edensor was far below my expectation. <br/><br/>Compare to LP, Edensor did not have strong character. The flow of building the conflict sound too harsh, too fast. In LP Andrea has capability to bring the reader up and down emotionally through beautiful words, careful sentences and so poetic. Even LP -as Andrea admitted only his memoir but it did have details that enrich the story.</span>
  <span id="freeText12448587451394266578" style="display:none">I read Edensor after the first tetra-logy of Andrea Hirata Laskar Pelangi (LP). Only take few hours I came to conclusions that Edensor was far below my expectation. <br /><br />Compare to LP, Edensor did not have strong character. The flow of building the conflict sound too harsh, too fast. In LP Andrea has capability to bring the reader up and down emotionally through beautiful words, careful sentences and so poetic. Even LP -as Andrea admitted only his memoir but it did have details that enrich the story.<br /><br />Edensor lacked of those details. It has potential to be as good as LP. I smelt something missing here, something that supposed to explain many things about his journey.<br /><br />I do love the way he explain his admire to Weh but then I can not find any better than that. Ah Ling -the girl that he's been chasing through internet googling was naive indeed but so touching. I felt the same way when you only love the one like Arai did. <br /><br />Hope the last tetra-logy Maryamah Karpov will answer all my curiosity. Edensor still worth to read but I was hoping even better than that.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12448587451394266578" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2865270347799966037">Hirata interpret that childhood dreams are meant to be realized; just dare to dream. Life is good when you have people who are supporting your dreams and believing in them too. The author also describe life as pieces of mozek, waiting to be discovered and connected. Overall, I am moved and inspire with the storyline.</span>

<div id="review_80380481" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/80380481" />
    <a title="Kit" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2310268-kit"><img alt="Kit" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1251048937p2/2310268.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/80380481?book_show_action=true">Dec 08, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kit" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kit" href="/user/show/2310268-kit">Kit</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/11427330-edensor">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer80380481" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6051129720425160635">OH WOW<br/><br/>The book, on its own, is praiseworthy, a masterpiece, and so on and so forth. Edensor has a more international feel than its predecessors which is only natural, as the protagonist(s) packed their bags for Europe, but it is an absolute tou-de-force: It is breakneck speed literature which drags you, well pretty damn fast, although you offer yourself willingly; struggle to keep up as you travel from the frostbitten plum trees of Russia to the sparse heartlands of Africa. But no, you will keep</span>
  <span id="freeText6051129720425160635" style="display:none">OH WOW<br /><br />The book, on its own, is praiseworthy, a masterpiece, and so on and so forth. Edensor has a more international feel than its predecessors which is only natural, as the protagonist(s) packed their bags for Europe, but it is an absolute tou-de-force: It is breakneck speed literature which drags you, well pretty damn fast, although you offer yourself willingly; struggle to keep up as you travel from the frostbitten plum trees of Russia to the sparse heartlands of Africa. But no, you will keep up, just because the protagonist's madness for life, which believe me, will rub on to you too. <br /><br />A couple of things stood out.<br /><br />Hirata's integrity: Travel literature is often plagued by authors who have been there done that and as a result lose the integrity of their stories. Their tone, as much as they can't help it, becomes arrogant. The journey of the two village boys from Belitung shame most travel literature which have lost track of their modesty. Ikal is irresistible, for me, simply because he is a humble narrator.<br /><br />The motif of travelling: the usual servings of self-discovery, spiritualism, survival, are all here compacted inside 150 pages (the last half of the book), but Ikal's motivation is driven by the need to find the mythical "A Ling", the one that got away, Edensor personified.<br /><br />But the book for me contains sentimental value. Any backpacker can relate straight away. This book resonates for travellers and would be travellers because of that unwritten backpacker code of ethics: respect and storytelling. No doubt, this is the Indonesian "On the Road" and will spark a generation of Indonesian youths conquering Europe all the way to Africa, and back again.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6051129720425160635" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText14312510577340871317" style="display:none">The third book of the tetralogy 'Laskar Pelangi' that I read. <span id="freeTextContainer10278546708878787784">This is the third series of Laskar Pelangi tetralogy. For this book, I decided to write its review in English… Why? Because the setting was not in Indonesia, the book was about Andrea and Arai’s journey in Europe. <br/><br/>In the previous book, Sang Pemimpi, Andrea and Arai got the scholarship they had been dreaming of… they were going to study at Sorbonne in France.<br/><br/>Andrea wrote Edensor in a different way compare to Laskar Pelangi and Sang Pemimpi.   <span id="freeText10278546708878787784" style="display:none">This is the third series of Laskar Pelangi tetralogy. For this book, I decided to write its review in English… Why? Because the setting was not in Indonesia, the book was about Andrea and Arai’s journey in Europe. <br /><br />In the previous book, Sang Pemimpi, Andrea and Arai got the scholarship they had been dreaming of… they were going to study at Sorbonne in France.<br /><br />Andrea wrote Edensor in a different way compare to Laskar Pelangi and Sang Pemimpi. The book was written in separated mosaics…at first it felt like separated but in the end we will learn that all those mosaics were connected in a certain way. But it still had the sense of comedy and irony like the previous books. Edensor showed us that Andrea has the ability to write in different style without losing his redline.<br /><br />the rest of the review <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://bokunosekai.wordpress.com/2009/01/10/edensor/">http://bokunosekai.wordpress.com/2009...</a></span>

Mbuatku merasa ga pantas dapat beasiswa juga siy, karena masih banyak orang cerdas yg lebih pantas mdapatkannya hanya karena nasib tidak berpihak pada mereka. Benarlah kata orang: life doesn't always go to a stronger or faster person, but the man who wins is the man who thinks he can</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('iXAwYM1lYVpfcQ+orVqnZexpkkIzFQcsEvRnz4Mazy+GkxelYHgIezPvHLcVgmRTgS36LowRXNvVpQel+NXdbA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Rv3kwJbu8h5/HOiNETWkwyQaRrQv7w/4b+iLpkOt9CxJHsMFO/ObPxOC+5Kp7Wf1SV4u2JDrVA+ouevMOGLmbw==')})
  }

Yang mereka tahu adalah: Jangan pernah remehkan impian, walau setinggi apa pun. Tuhan sungguh Maha Mendengar.\n\nBagaimana perjalanan mereka ke ujung dunia ini dimulai? Siapa horor nomor satu mereka? Kesejatian hidup ada pada selembar daun kering yang gugur\ntertiup angin. Kesejatian hidup ada air susu ibu yang yang merelakan puting\npayudaranya diisap oleh bayi manapun. Di\nVihara Pit Yong Kiong, Pasuruan, di pelabuhan Belawan, di Penang, di\nBangkok, di Laos, di Golden Triangle, di Cambodia, di Bandung, di\nmanapun kau hidup.\n\nTapi, dia mungkin tak terlihat pada arus politik yang menyudutkanmu pada\npilihan kedigdayaan. Dia menyembunyikan diri dari teriakan-\nteriakan yang menggemakan perubahan. Kesejatian hidup tak memerlukan\nperubahan, namun juga tak menampiknya. Dia rebah pada semua kesederhanaan\nyang ada di sekelilingmu. Maka, carilah, dan kamu akan mendapatinya.\nKetuklah, maka pintu akan dibukakan bagimu. Mintalah, maka kau akan diberi.\n\nDemikianlah Dewi Lestari mewakilkan sebuah upaya pencarian kesejatian hidup\npada seorang tokoh bernama Bodhi. Seorang bayi yang di suatu pagi tergeletak\ndi pintu Vihara. Dipungut, diasuh, dan dididik oleh seorang Pandita, Guru\nLiong. Merasa bahwa karma pada hidup masa lalunya sangat berat. 18 tahun\ndididik dengan ketat, termasuk penguasaan terhadap sebuah ilmu bela diri,\nBodhi mengalami penyempurnaan bathin. Pemurnian spirit. Termasuk sejumlah\npengalaman uniknya yang &quot;merasa&quot; menjadi ulat, tikus got, kucing, dan sapi.\n\n18 tahun adalah waktu yang cukup, dan Bodhi mohon pamit. Bersama serombongan\npendeta Buddha, Bodhi menyeberang ke Sumatera dan memutuskan menetap di\ndaerah Belawan. Tanpa KTP, tak juga faham mengenai asal usul dan tanggal\nkelahirannya. Bekerja tiga bulan, mendapat upah, dan dibantu oleh Ompu\nBerlin untuk mendapatkan sejumlah dokumen identitas termasuk paspor, Bodhi\nmenyeberang ke Penang. Disana dia bertemu dengan sejumlah backpackers yang\nkemudian &quot;memberi&quot; arah perjalanan berikutnya: Bangkok.\n\nBangkok surga bagi para backpackers. Ratusan pengelana dari mancanegara\ntumpah di sana. Bodhi tinggal di semua rumah penginapan Srinthip bersama\nsejumlah backpakers multi etnis. Penghuninya datang dan pergi. Masuklah\nKell, seorang lelaki tampan, peranakan Irlandia dan Mesir. Lelaki tertampan\nyang mungkin pernah ada di bumi ini yang mempunyai tugas kehidupan untuk\nmembubuhkan 617 tatto pada 617 orang untuk membuat dirinya menyongsong\nkemerdekaan paripurna setelah orang ke-617 membubuhkan tato yang ke-618 ke\ntubuhnya. Lelaki yang kerap menyenandungkan Eye in The Sky-nya Alan Parson\nProject. Kell kemudian mengajarinya tattoo. Lalu, jadilah Bodhi seorang\ntattooist dan menjadikan itu sebagai cara untuk mendapatkan uang bagi biaya\nhidup sehari-hari.\n\nSeorang backpacker perempuan bernama Star, berasal dari Hollywood, peranakan\nEropa Timur dan Timur Tengah masuk dan menginap di Srinthip. Perempuan\ncantik dan tercantik yang pernah dilihat Bodhi. Perawakan tubuhnya sempurna.\nPerempuan inilah yang memperkenalkan dirinya dengan sebuah perasaan lain\nyang belum pernah dia rasakan sepanjang hidup. Star minta Bodhi mentattoonya\ntepat di payudara.Dan bergetarlah kulit semesta. Bergerolalah gelombang\nsamudera. Erangan kesakitan Star sewaktu ditattoo adalah hasrat dedaunan\nyang mendambakan sapuan sinar matahari. Waktu berlalu dan mereka berpisah.\nEntah kenapa.\n\nBodhi meneruskan pencarian kesejatiannya. Star seolah menggenap kesempurnaan\ntattoonya dan pergi menyongsong kelana berikut.\nKeterserakan yang tak menyenangkan. Tapi hidup adalah keping-keping misteri\nyang baru terbuka setelah rebah sepenuhnya. Bodhi membiarkan semesta\nmenuntun perjalanan selanjutnya. Bertemu dengan lelaki tua pengasuh Bob\nMarley, yang mengumandangkan reggae seolah cuma itu yang ada di bumi dan\nkahyangan. Bertemu kembali dengan Tristan, backpacker yang ditemuinya\npertama kali di Penang. Mereka berdua bekerja di ladang ganja di Golden\nTriangle dengan upah USD 700 per minggu. Sekian bulan di sana Bodhi memiliki\ncukup uang untuk melanjutkan kembara berikutnya. Pulang ke Srinthip\ndidapatinya Kell sudah tak ada. Ah, lelaki yang telah memberinya keceriaan\ndan sebuah warna baru.\n\nRasa kangennya memuncak. Diputuskannya untuk pergi mencari Kell. Tak ada\npetunjuk. Tak ada berita. Dan dia pergi. Suara semesta dan kerinduannya\nadalah dua buah kompas sejati yang dia percaya akan mengantarkannya tepat\nwaktu - tepat arah kepada Kell. Bodhi terdampar di sebuah pertarungan antar\nmanusia ala Golden Triangle ditonton oleh ribuan petaruh. Diadu secara\nbarbar di atas ring melawan gladiator raksasa. Pertarungan dahsyat dengan\nmenggunakan sejumlah jurus wushu yang mendebarkan pun digelar.\n\nPerjalanan itu begitu panjang dan melelahkan. Menembus belukar di antara\ndesingan peluru. Menyusuri daratan ranjau. Disana dia betemu Epona, gadis\npenakluk ranjau. Disana pula ia bertemu kembali dengan Kell. Lalu, pada\nsebuah kunjungan ke lokasi ranjau, tattoo ke 618, angka kebebasan paripurna\nKell, dirajahkan. Dalam dialog cerdas, konyol, menggelikan, dan bertabur air\nmata. Adegan mengejutkan, dan merupakan bagian terindah. Kebebasan itu\ndatang dan menyapa dalam damai. Nikmati adegan ini sambil mendengarkan You\nTake My Breath Away-nya QUEEN. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer3631243365973578801">Under a bright sunny sky, the three-day Byron Bay Writers’ Festival welcomed Andrea Hirata who charmed audiences with his modesty and gracious behavior during two sessions. <br/><br/>Andrea also attended a special event where he and Tim Baker, an Australian surfing writer, spoke to a gathering of several hundred school children. During one session, Andrea was on a panel with Pulitzer Prize winning journalis</span>
  <span id="freeText3631243365973578801" style="display:none">Under a bright sunny sky, the three-day Byron Bay Writers’ Festival welcomed Andrea Hirata who charmed audiences with his modesty and gracious behavior during two sessions. <br /><br />Andrea also attended a special event where he and Tim Baker, an Australian surfing writer, spoke to a gathering of several hundred school children. During one session, Andrea was on a panel with Pulitzer Prize winning journalist from Washington, DC, Katharine Boo, which he said was a great honor.<br /><br />The August event for the school children was very meaningful to Andrea, the barefooted boy from <br />Belitung, as he made mental comparisons with the educational opportunities of these children, compared to what he experienced. <br /><br />And now his own life story is about to become even more amazing, as his book Laskar Pelangi (The Rainbow Troops) is being published around the world in no less than twenty-four countries and in 12 languages. It has caught the eye of some of the world’s top publishing houses, such as Penguin, Random House, Farrar, Straus and Giroux, (New York, US) and many others. Translations are already on sale in Brazil, Taiwan, South Korea and Malaysia. <br /><br />All this has come about because of the feeling of appreciation that the young Andrea felt for his teacher, Muslimah. He promised her that he’d write a book for her someday. This was because for him and his school friends, a book was the most valuable thing they could think of. <br /><br />Andrea told a story that illustrated this fact. When royalties flowed in for him he decided to give his community a library. He spent a lot of money on books. He left the village headman in charge of administering the library. However, when he came back several months later, all the books were gone. People loved the books, but they had no concept of how a lending library functioned. <br /><br />“Some of them could not even read, but they just loved to have a book, an object of great value and importance, in their homes. We will restock the library with books and this time it will be run by our own administration,” he laughed.<br /><br />Andrea told this story as we sat in the coffee shop adjoining a Gold Coast City Library, one of 12 scattered around the city. One of the librarians, Jenneth Duque, showed him around the library, including the new state-of-the-art book sorting machine, for processing returns located in the staff area. As he saw the books being returned through pigeonholes by the borrowers and the computerized conveyor belt sorting them into the correct bin for reshelving, the sight made him laugh and prompted the telling of that story.<br /><br />Andrea wrote the book for his teacher while in the employ of Telkom, but the completed manuscript was taken from his room, which was located in a Bandung student accommodation community. Whoever took the manuscript knew enough to send it to a publisher and that’s how Andrea, an unhappy postal service worker who had studied economics in Europe and the UK, became the accidental author of the biggest selling novel in Indonesia’s history.<br /><br />He has since written seven more books. <br /><br />Fast forward to 2011 and Andrea was in Iowa, the US, where he did a reading of his short story, The Dry Season. He was approached by an independent literary agent, Kathleen Anderson. They talked, but for six months there was no news until an email arrived telling him that one of the best publishers in the US, Farrar, Straus and Giroux, had accepted his book. <br /><br />Then every week, more publishers said “yes” and now he has 24 contracts from the world’s leading publishers.<br /><br />Andrea worked with Angie Kilbane of the US on the English translations of Laskar Pelangi and its sequel Sang Pemimpi (The Dreamer). Translators from several other countries have visited his home village in Belitung to do research. <br /><br />“For a long time I wondered what was the key to the enormous success of my book,” Andrea said. <br /><br />“I think there’s no single right answer. Perhaps people are fed up with writing focused on urban issues or esca</span>
